Karl Wisdom <k.j.hirner.wisdom@gmail.com>
Possible Scammer Website
Karl Wisdom <k.j.hirner.wisdom@gmail.com>Tue, Jan 9, 2018 at 11:44 PM
To: email@godaddy.com, Karl Wisdom <k.j.hirner.wisdom@gmail.com>
To whom this may concern,

During a recent web search, I came across a scammer website that threatens to lock up the users personal computer. Through the use of a few Linux utilities, I managed to identify that the address that this scammer's website runs through your systems. No regular user should have to come across this website. I have appended the data as a base64 encapsulated zip string to the end of this email, as well as to provide them below. Additionally, I have also provided the index.html file for this particular site. If you have access to a Linux system use `echo $data | base64 -d - > scammer-shutdown.zip` where $data is the base64 string at the end of this email. Do not include the double quotes in this email when decoding this data. The data will also be posted on my github in source file, and zip file form. I have also included the data in a text file, similar to the data provided in this email, but will require some work to extract, as Gmail's Virus detection will not allow a base64 file pass through. Below I have provided the de-modification process.

De-modification process is as follows, given that a Linux machine with base64 and the ability to handle zip files is provided.

`cat scammer-shutdown-sed_modded.txt | sed s/\"//g | base64 -d - > scammer-shutdown.zip`

The above process takes advantage of the fact the base64 does not include the \" character in its character set, and that Gmail does not scan for malformed base64 files.
